## Step 3: Spawn PM Agent

The PM agent handles scoping, GitHub Issues, and task graph creation. It does NOT spawn other agents — only the orchestrator can spawn agents.

```
Task {
  name: "pm-agent",
  subagent_type: "product-manager",
  team_name: "feat-<slugified-arguments>",
  prompt: "You are the PM for this feature team.

FEATURE REQUEST: Dispatch discoverability — inline "Write about this" entry point on InsightsPage + dismissible discovery callout + pre-populated DispatchDrawer from session facets.

Design decisions locked by UX Engineer:

ENHANCEMENT 1 — Inline entry button:
- Component: DispatchEntryButton.tsx in dashboard/src/components/insights/
- shadcn Button variant="outline" size="sm" with Lucide PenLine icon
- Visible only for session types: feature_build, deep_focus, bug_hunt, refactor — hidden entirely (not disabled) for other types
- Placed trailing edge of InsightsPage header action row alongside existing Rename/Open buttons
- Hidden when facets are undefined (analysis not yet run)
- On click: opens DispatchDrawer with prefill, sets localStorage ci.dispatch.opened = "1"

ENHANCEMENT 2 — Dismissible discovery callout:
- Component: DispatchDiscoveryCallout.tsx in dashboard/src/components/insights/
- Full-width strip below header, above tabs: rounded-lg border bg-muted/40 px-4 py-3 mb-4
- Sparkles icon (text-primary) + "Turn this session into a writeup" heading + subtitle copy
- Three actions: "Try it" (Button size="sm" default — opens drawer + dismisses), "Not now" (Button size="sm" variant="ghost" — dismisses), X close icon button
- Visibility rules: hidden if localStorage ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed === "1" OR ci.dispatch.opened === "1" OR facets not yet loaded
- Dismiss: set ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed = "1", fade out (transition-opacity duration-150)
- Hook: useDispatchDiscovery.ts wrapping localStorage reads/writes, returns { shouldShowCallout, markCalloutDismissed, markDispatchOpened }

ENHANCEMENT 3 — Pre-populated DispatchDrawer:
- New type: DispatchPrefill { sessionId, title, format, contextMarkdown } in dashboard/src/lib/types.ts (or api.ts)
- New pure function: buildDispatchPrefill(session, facets): DispatchPrefill — testable, decoupled
- Pre-fill logic:
  - title: session.title
  - format: feature_build→Tutorial, bug_hunt→Postmortem, refactor→Technical deep-dive, deep_focus→Technical deep-dive
  - contextMarkdown: "What you learned\n- {pattern[0..2].description}\n\nWhat was hard\n- {friction[0..2].description}" — cap 3 patterns, 3 user-actionable friction only (attribution === 'user-actionable'), omit section heading if empty
- DispatchDrawer: accept optional prefill?: DispatchPrefill prop; when present, pre-fill title input (with text selected on open via autoFocus), pre-select format, populate context textarea
- "Reset to defaults" ghost button below textarea — appears only after user edits textarea, restores templated prefill on click
- When opened from InsightsPage: header subtitle "Drafting from {session.title}" (text-xs text-muted-foreground)

Modified files: InsightsPage.tsx (mount drawer + button + callout, thread state), DispatchDrawer.tsx (accept prefill prop, subtitle, reset-to-defaults)
New files: DispatchEntryButton.tsx, DispatchDiscoveryCallout.tsx, useDispatchDiscovery.ts, buildDispatchPrefill.ts (or co-located pure fn)
No changes: API routes, SQLite schema, CLI, server, other dashboard pages

Telemetry events (add to existing PostHog calls):
- dispatch.discovery_callout_shown
- dispatch.discovery_callout_dismissed (with via: 'x' | 'not_now' | 'try_it')
- dispatch.opened_from_insights (with session_character)

Scope boundary (do not build): publish integrations, inline editing of generated post, format picker changes, session picker changes.
WORKTREE: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/
BRANCH: feature/<slugified-arguments>
TEAM: feat-<slugified-arguments>

Your responsibilities are scoping, GitHub Issues, task graph, and handoff preparation.
IMPORTANT: You CANNOT spawn agents. Only the orchestrator can. When you need an agent spawned, message the orchestrator with the request.

Follow this protocol:

1. SCOPE: Read docs in docs/ and CLAUDE.md to understand what this feature involves. Check for existing design docs in docs/plans/. Check docs/architecture/ for architecture context. If the scope is unclear, message the orchestrator for clarification.

2. ISSUES: Search for an existing GitHub Issue that matches this feature. If one exists, use it. If not, create one with proper description, acceptance criteria, and T-shirt size. Record the issue number.

3. TASK GRAPH: Create the ceremony tasks using TaskCreate, then set dependencies with TaskUpdate:
   - Task: 'TA: Review architecture alignment' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if internal-only (new components, UI, styling)
   - Task: 'LLM Expert: Design prompt architecture' (no dependencies) -- SKIP if feature doesn't involve LLM calls
   - Task: 'PM: Prepare handoff context in GitHub Issue' (no dependencies, you do this yourself)
   - Task: 'Dev: Read handoff and design docs, prepare questions' (blockedBy: TA + LLM Expert if applicable + PM handoff)
   - Task: 'Dev + TA: Reach consensus on implementation approach' (blockedBy: above) -- SKIP if internal-only
   - Task: 'Dev: Implement feature in worktree' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Dev: Verify feature and create PR' (blockedBy: above) -- includes pre-PR verification protocol
   - Task: 'Review: Triple-layer code review (loops until 0 FIX NOW)' (blockedBy: above)
   - Task: 'Post final review summary to GitHub PR' (blockedBy: above)

4. DO YOUR OWN TASK: Work on your handoff task -- prepare context in the GitHub Issue (description, acceptance criteria, relevant doc paths, implementation guidance).

   IMPORTANT — Classify the feature scope for Dev's verification protocol:
   - Does it touch UI/visual rendering? → Tag: VISUAL
   - Does it produce output artifacts (images, PDFs, exports)? → Tag: OUTPUT_ARTIFACT
   - Does it add new npm dependencies? → Tag: NEW_DEPS
   - Does it change API endpoints? → Tag: API_CHANGE
   Include these tags in the GitHub Issue so Dev knows which verification tiers apply.

5. REQUEST AGENT SPAWNS: When your handoff task is done, message the orchestrator:
   - If TA is needed: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: ta-agent — [brief context]'
   - When dev prerequisites are met: 'SPAWN_REQUEST: dev-agent — [brief context including issue number and key details]'
   The orchestrator will spawn the agents and assign tasks.

   SKIP TA if the feature is internal-only (new components, UI fixes, styling, LLM provider additions). In that case, mark the TA task as completed with note 'Skipped -- internal-only change'.

   If the feature involves LLM calls (prompts, model selection, token budgets, structured output):
   - 'SPAWN_REQUEST: llm-expert-agent — [brief context about the LLM aspect]'
   The LLM Expert will design the prompt architecture, token budget, and model recommendation before dev implements.

   SKIP LLM Expert if the feature doesn't touch LLM code. Mark the task as completed with note 'Skipped -- no LLM impact'.

6. MONITOR: Check TaskList periodically.
   - When Dev creates a PR, message the orchestrator: 'REVIEW_REQUEST: PR #XX is ready for /start-review'
   - The orchestrator will run /start-review which loops until 0 FIX NOW items
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, the orchestrator sends them to Dev. Dev fixes and pushes. Review re-runs automatically.
   - You do NOT need to request additional review rounds — the loop is built into /start-review.

7. REPORT: When review converges (0 FIX NOW items) and final summary is posted, message the orchestrator: 'PR #XX for Dispatch discoverability — inline "Write about this" entry point on InsightsPage + dismissible discovery callout + pre-populated DispatchDrawer from session facets.

Design decisions locked by UX Engineer:

ENHANCEMENT 1 — Inline entry button:
- Component: DispatchEntryButton.tsx in dashboard/src/components/insights/
- shadcn Button variant="outline" size="sm" with Lucide PenLine icon
- Visible only for session types: feature_build, deep_focus, bug_hunt, refactor — hidden entirely (not disabled) for other types
- Placed trailing edge of InsightsPage header action row alongside existing Rename/Open buttons
- Hidden when facets are undefined (analysis not yet run)
- On click: opens DispatchDrawer with prefill, sets localStorage ci.dispatch.opened = "1"

ENHANCEMENT 2 — Dismissible discovery callout:
- Component: DispatchDiscoveryCallout.tsx in dashboard/src/components/insights/
- Full-width strip below header, above tabs: rounded-lg border bg-muted/40 px-4 py-3 mb-4
- Sparkles icon (text-primary) + "Turn this session into a writeup" heading + subtitle copy
- Three actions: "Try it" (Button size="sm" default — opens drawer + dismisses), "Not now" (Button size="sm" variant="ghost" — dismisses), X close icon button
- Visibility rules: hidden if localStorage ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed === "1" OR ci.dispatch.opened === "1" OR facets not yet loaded
- Dismiss: set ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed = "1", fade out (transition-opacity duration-150)
- Hook: useDispatchDiscovery.ts wrapping localStorage reads/writes, returns { shouldShowCallout, markCalloutDismissed, markDispatchOpened }

ENHANCEMENT 3 — Pre-populated DispatchDrawer:
- New type: DispatchPrefill { sessionId, title, format, contextMarkdown } in dashboard/src/lib/types.ts (or api.ts)
- New pure function: buildDispatchPrefill(session, facets): DispatchPrefill — testable, decoupled
- Pre-fill logic:
  - title: session.title
  - format: feature_build→Tutorial, bug_hunt→Postmortem, refactor→Technical deep-dive, deep_focus→Technical deep-dive
  - contextMarkdown: "What you learned\n- {pattern[0..2].description}\n\nWhat was hard\n- {friction[0..2].description}" — cap 3 patterns, 3 user-actionable friction only (attribution === 'user-actionable'), omit section heading if empty
- DispatchDrawer: accept optional prefill?: DispatchPrefill prop; when present, pre-fill title input (with text selected on open via autoFocus), pre-select format, populate context textarea
- "Reset to defaults" ghost button below textarea — appears only after user edits textarea, restores templated prefill on click
- When opened from InsightsPage: header subtitle "Drafting from {session.title}" (text-xs text-muted-foreground)

Modified files: InsightsPage.tsx (mount drawer + button + callout, thread state), DispatchDrawer.tsx (accept prefill prop, subtitle, reset-to-defaults)
New files: DispatchEntryButton.tsx, DispatchDiscoveryCallout.tsx, useDispatchDiscovery.ts, buildDispatchPrefill.ts (or co-located pure fn)
No changes: API routes, SQLite schema, CLI, server, other dashboard pages

Telemetry events (add to existing PostHog calls):
- dispatch.discovery_callout_shown
- dispatch.discovery_callout_dismissed (with via: 'x' | 'not_now' | 'try_it')
- dispatch.opened_from_insights (with session_character)

Scope boundary (do not build): publish integrations, inline editing of generated post, format picker changes, session picker changes. is ready for founder review and merge.'

IMPORTANT RULES:
- NEVER merge PRs -- founder-only
- NEVER try to spawn agents -- message the orchestrator instead
- All dev work happens in the worktree
- If you need user clarification, message the orchestrator who will ask the user
- You can message existing teammates directly via SendMessage for routine coordination
- Task dependencies enforce ceremony order -- don't skip steps
- PRE-PR GATE (MANDATORY): Before any PR is created, Dev must complete the full verification protocol (see Dev agent instructions). GitHub Actions costs money — failed CI runs are wasted spend.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

- Full-width strip below header, above tabs: rounded-lg border bg-muted/40 px-4 py-3 mb-4
- Sparkles icon (text-primary) + "Turn this session into a writeup" heading + subtitle copy

- Visibility rules: hidden if localStorage ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed === "1" OR ci.dispatch.opened === "1" OR facets not yet loaded
- Dismiss: set ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed = "1", fade out (transition-opacity duration-150)
- Hook: useDispatchDiscovery.ts wrapping localStorage reads/writes, returns { shouldShowCallout, markCalloutDismissed, markDispatchOpened }

Modified files: InsightsPage.tsx (mount drawer + button + callout, thread state), DispatchDrawer.tsx (accept prefill prop, subtitle, reset-to-defaults)

No changes: API routes, SQLite schema, CLI, server, other dashboard pages

Scope boundary (do not build): publish integrations, inline editing of generated post, format picker changes, session picker changes.. Worktree: ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>/. All code work happens in the worktree. Check TaskList for your tasks. Use SendMessage to communicate with pm-agent. Mark tasks in_progress/completed.

## Pre-PR Verification Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before creating any PR, you MUST complete ALL applicable verification tiers. Check the GitHub Issue for scope tags (VISUAL, OUTPUT_ARTIFACT, NEW_DEPS, API_CHANGE) to know which tiers apply.

### Tier 1: Build & Test (ALWAYS required)
1. Run `pnpm build` from the worktree repo root — must pass with zero errors
2. Run `pnpm test` from cli/ — must pass
3. If build or tests fail, fix before proceeding. Do NOT create the PR.

### Tier 2: New Dependency Audit (required if NEW_DEPS tag)
If you added any new npm dependencies:
1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations and common gotchas
2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility, and unsupported features
3. Specifically check for: CSS compatibility, serialization constraints, SSR issues, bundle size impact
4. Document findings in the PR description under '## Dependency Audit'
5. If you find high-risk limitations, verify your code handles them correctly

### Tier 3: Functional Verification (required if VISUAL or API_CHANGE tag)
You must verify the feature works by running it:

**Server access:**
1. First, check if the dev server is already running: `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}' http://localhost:7890/api/health` (or just `http://localhost:7890`)
2. If the server responds (200), use the existing server — do NOT start a new one
3. If the server is NOT running, start one:
   ```bash
   cd <worktree-path> && node cli/dist/index.js dashboard --no-sync &
   DEV_SERVER_PID=$!
   ```
4. CRITICAL: If you started a server, you MUST kill it when done: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID`
5. NEVER leave orphaned server processes running

**For UI features (VISUAL tag):**
- Navigate to the affected page using agent-browser tools
- Take a screenshot showing the feature renders correctly
- Attach the screenshot to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For output-producing features (OUTPUT_ARTIFACT tag):**
- Trigger the feature (e.g., click download, run export)
- Verify the output file exists and is non-empty
- If it's a visual artifact (image, PDF), take a screenshot of the output
- Attach evidence to the PR description under '## Verification'

**For API changes (API_CHANGE tag):**
- curl the new/modified endpoints
- Verify the response shape matches the TypeScript types
- Include the curl output in the PR description under '## Verification'

### Tier 4: Cleanup
- If you started a dev server, confirm it's killed: `kill $DEV_SERVER_PID 2>/dev/null`
- Verify no orphaned node processes on port 7890: `lsof -ti:7890` (should return nothing, or only the user's existing server)

## PR Description Template

Your PR description MUST include these sections:

```markdown
## Summary
[What this PR does]

## Dependency Audit (if NEW_DEPS)
[Library name]: [Known limitations found, or 'No significant limitations found']

## Verification
- Build: PASS
- Tests: PASS
- [Screenshot of feature rendering] (if VISUAL)
- [Screenshot/proof of output artifact] (if OUTPUT_ARTIFACT)
- [curl output] (if API_CHANGE)

## Test plan
- [ ] [Checklist of what to test]
```

## During Review Rounds

If the review team sends back FIX NOW items:
1. Read each item carefully
2. Implement the fixes in the worktree
3. Re-run applicable verification tiers (at minimum Tier 1)
4. If fixes are visual, re-capture screenshots
5. Push the fix commits to the PR branch
6. Message pm-agent that fixes are pushed

This is non-negotiable — thorough pre-PR verification prevents wasted review cycles and catches bugs that static code review cannot.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```
Assign the next unblocked dev task to dev-agent.

---

## Step 5: Supervise

After spawning agents, your role is active supervisor:

1. **PM handles scoping and task graph** — orchestrator handles all agent spawning
2. **Spawn agents when PM sends SPAWN_REQUEST messages**
3. **Intervene when**:
   - PM messages you asking for user clarification -> relay to user
   - An agent is stuck or reports a blocker -> help unblock
   - PM sends a REVIEW_REQUEST -> run `/start-review` on the PR number
4. **Review loop management**:
   - `/start-review` handles the loop internally (runs rounds until 0 FIX NOW items)
   - If review finds FIX NOW items, relay them to the dev-agent via SendMessage
   - After dev pushes fixes, `/start-review` re-runs targeted reviewers automatically
   - If review hits max rounds (4) without converging, escalate to user
5. **When PM reports "ready for merge"** -> inform the user

---

## Step 6: Cleanup (After PR Merge)

After the founder merges the PR:

1. Send shutdown requests to all teammates (pm-agent, ta-agent, dev-agent)
2. Delete the team: `TeamDelete`
3. Clean up worktree:
```bash
git worktree remove ../code-insights-<slugified-arguments>
```
4. Confirm cleanup is complete

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** — founder-only
- **Only the orchestrator spawns agents** — sub-agents CANNOT use the Task tool to spawn teammates. PM must send SPAWN_REQUEST messages to the orchestrator.
- **PM handles scoping and coordination** — it creates task graphs, GitHub Issues, and prepares handoff context
- **Orchestrator is the agent factory** — spawns TA and Dev agents when PM requests them
- **All dev work happens in the worktree**
- **Task dependencies enforce ceremony order** — agents can't skip steps
- **TA is optional** for internal-only changes — PM decides based on scope
- **Dev must complete pre-PR verification** — build, test, functional check, dependency audit (as applicable)
- **Review loops automatically** — orchestrator runs /start-review which iterates until convergence
- **No orphaned processes** — dev agent must kill any server it starts

# /start-review — Triple-Layer Code Review Team

**PR**: 301

You are setting up a triple-layer code review for PR `301`. This can be used standalone or as part of a `/start-feature` team workflow. The review loops until all FIX NOW items are resolved — it does NOT end after a single pass.

---

## Step 1: Get PR Details

Fetch the PR details:

```bash
# Get the correct owner from git remote
git remote get-url origin | sed 's/.*[:/]\([^/]*\)\/[^/]*\.git/\1/'
```

Use `gh pr view 301` to get PR title, description, and diff stats.
Use `gh pr diff 301` to get the diff.

Determine the PR scope:
- Count files changed and lines changed per file
- Identify if it touches schema concerns (types.ts, SQLite schema, server API)
- Classify changed files into domains for specialist selection (Step 2)

---

## Step 2: Select Domain Specialists

Instead of fixed generalist reviewers, select 1-2 **domain specialists** based on what the PR actually changes. Each specialist combines deep domain expertise with general engineering awareness. See `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md` for the full specialist registry and prompt templates.

### Domain Classification

Classify each changed file into a domain based on file patterns:

| Domain | File Pattern Triggers |
|--------|----------------------|
| **SQL/Database** | `server/src/routes/*.ts` (when containing SQL keywords), `cli/src/db/*.ts` |
| **React/Frontend** | `dashboard/src/**/*.tsx`, `dashboard/src/**/*.ts` |
| **Node/CLI** | `cli/src/commands/*.ts`, `cli/src/utils/*.ts`, `server/src/*.ts` (non-route, non-LLM) |
| **Parser/Provider** | `cli/src/providers/**/*.ts`, `cli/src/parser/*.ts` |
| **LLM** | `server/src/llm/**/*.ts` — handled by LLM Expert (separate, unchanged) |

Files that don't match any domain (e.g., `package.json`, `tsconfig.json`, `.gitignore`, `CLAUDE.md`) are ignored during classification.

### Selection Algorithm

1. For each domain, sum the lines changed across all files in that domain
2. **Primary specialist** = domain with the most lines changed
3. **Secondary specialist** = next domain IF it has >= 30% of total changed lines AND is a different domain
4. Cap at **2 domain specialists** (LLM Expert is a separate conditional reviewer)
5. If a PR changes ONLY non-domain files, use the **Node/CLI Specialist** as general-purpose

### LLM Expert (Conditional — Unchanged)

**Invoke LLM Expert if ANY of these apply:**
- PR touches `server/src/llm/` (prompts, providers, export-prompts)
- PR adds or modifies LLM API calls
- PR changes structured output schemas or SSE streaming
- PR modifies token budgets or model selection logic
- PR adds new LLM-powered features

**Skip LLM Expert if ALL of these apply:**
- No LLM code touched
- Pure UI, CLI, or schema changes
- Provider (source tool) implementations only

---

## Step 2.5: Pre-Review Gates

Before launching reviewers, check these gates. If any gate fails, the review CANNOT proceed — send the PR back to the dev agent (or inform the user if standalone) with what's missing.

### Gate A: New Dependency Audit

Check if `package.json` (any workspace) was modified in the PR diff.

If new dependencies were added:

```
Task {
  name: "dep-auditor",
  subagent_type: "Explore",
  prompt: "Research the following new npm dependencies added in PR #301. For EACH dependency:

  1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations, gotchas, and common pitfalls
  2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility notes, and unsupported features
  3. Check if the library has specific CSS, rendering, or serialization constraints
  4. Check the library's weekly downloads and last publish date (is it maintained?)

  Output a structured report:
  ## Dependency Audit: [package-name]
  ### Known Limitations
  ### Gotchas for Our Use Case
  ### Risk Level (low/medium/high)
  ### Recommendation

  Be thorough — silent failures from library limitations are the hardest bugs to catch in code review.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Include the dependency audit findings in the context given to ALL reviewers.

### Gate B: Functional Verification Evidence

Check the PR description for a **Verification** section. The dev agent is required to include:

- **For all PRs**: Build passes (`pnpm build` output or confirmation)
- **For UI/visual features**: Screenshot of the feature rendering in the browser
- **For features that produce output** (image export, PDF, file download): The actual output artifact or proof it's non-empty (file size, screenshot of result)
- **For API changes**: curl output showing the endpoint returns the expected response shape

If the PR description lacks verification evidence:
- **If part of /start-feature**: Message the dev agent via SendMessage: "PR is missing verification evidence. Add a Verification section to the PR description with [specific evidence needed]. See the pre-PR verification protocol."
- **If standalone**: Inform the user the PR needs verification evidence before review can proceed.

**Do NOT proceed to Step 3 until verification evidence is present.**

### Gate C: Visual Output Check (Conditional)

If the PR produces visual output (images, PDFs, charts, OG cards, share cards, exports):
- The exported/generated artifact MUST be attached to or linked from the PR description
- A reviewer must be able to visually inspect the output without running the code
- If missing, send PR back with: "This PR produces visual output — attach the generated artifact to the PR description."

---

## Step 3: Run Parallel Independent Reviews (Round N)

**CRITICAL**: All reviews run in parallel. No reviewer sees another's comments. This prevents bias.

Track the current round number. Round 1 is the initial review. Round 2+ are follow-up reviews after fixes.

**For Round 1**: Launch all applicable reviewers (TA Insider, Domain Specialist(s), LLM Expert if applicable).
**For Round 2+**: Launch only targeted reviewers — those whose prior findings had FIX NOW or VERIFY AT RUNTIME items that were addressed. Skip reviewers whose prior findings were all resolved or NOT APPLICABLE.

### Launch TA Insider Review (Always)

```
Task {
  name: "ta-reviewer",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  prompt: "You are performing a Phase 1 INSIDER review of PR #301 in the code-insights repo. This is review ROUND [N].

  Fetch the PR diff using: gh pr diff 301
  Also fetch the PR details: gh pr view 301

  Follow your Phase 1 review protocol:
  1. Read the PR description and any linked GitHub Issue
  2. Check if the change touches schema concerns (types.ts, SQLite schema)
  3. Review code against existing patterns in the codebase
  4. Check existing CLAUDE.md conventions compliance
  5. Verify data contract patterns are followed (if data flow changed)
  6. Check shadcn/ui and component conventions (if UI changes)

  ADDITIONAL CHECKS:
  7. If new dependencies were added, review the dependency audit findings: [INSERT DEP AUDIT IF APPLICABLE]
  8. If the PR produces visual output, verify the attached artifact looks correct
  9. Check that verification evidence in the PR description is credible (not just 'it works')

  [FOR ROUND 2+: Focus on verifying the fixes for these specific items from Round [N-1]: [LIST PRIOR FIX NOW ITEMS]. Also check that fixes didn't introduce new issues.]

  Output your review in the structured format:
  ## TA Review (Phase 1 - Insider): [PR Title] — Round [N]
  ### Architecture Alignment
  ### Issues Found (with priority markers: 🔴 FIX NOW, 🟡 SUGGESTION, 🔵 NOTE)
  ### Phase 1 Verdict

  DO NOT look at any other review comments. Your review must be independent.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

### Launch Domain Specialist Reviews (1-2, Dynamic)

For each selected specialist from Step 2, launch a review agent using the prompt template from `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md`. Use the `superpowers:code-reviewer` subagent type for all domain specialists.

**Important:** Copy the full prompt template from the specialist registry, including:
- The domain-specific checks (80% focus)
- The general engineering checks (20% focus)
- The **Runtime Verification Rule** (shared instruction — include verbatim)
- The Round 2+ fix verification instructions (if applicable)

```
Task {
  name: "[domain]-specialist",          // e.g., "sql-specialist", "react-specialist"
  subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer",
  prompt: "[FULL PROMPT FROM docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md FOR THE SELECTED DOMAIN]",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

**Example:** If Step 2 selected SQL/Database (primary) and React/Frontend (secondary), launch:

```
Task { name: "sql-specialist", subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer", prompt: "[SQL/Database prompt]", mode: "bypassPermissions" }
Task { name: "react-specialist", subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer", prompt: "[React/Frontend prompt]", mode: "bypassPermissions" }
```

### Launch LLM Expert Review (If Applicable — Unchanged)

```
Task {
  name: "llm-expert-reviewer",
  subagent_type: "llm-expert",
  prompt: "You are performing an independent LLM EXPERT review of PR #301 in the code-insights repo. This is review ROUND [N].

  Fetch the PR diff using: gh pr diff 301
  Also fetch the PR details: gh pr view 301

  Review all LLM-related code for:
  - Prompt quality: clarity, specificity, output format constraints
  - Token efficiency: redundant instructions, over-prompting, prompt stuffing
  - Output consistency: structured output schemas, JSON mode, enum enforcement
  - Model selection: is the chosen model appropriate for the task complexity?
  - Resilience: handling malformed LLM output, timeouts, retries, rate limits
  - Cross-model compatibility: prompts that only work with one model family
  - Cost implications: token budget estimates, unnecessary Opus/GPT-4 usage for simple tasks
  - Streaming patterns: SSE implementation, partial response handling

  Rate each prompt on: clarity (1-5), token efficiency (1-5), output consistency (1-5), resilience (1-5).

  RUNTIME VERIFICATION RULE:
  When you encounter code where the runtime behavior is NOT self-evident from
  reading — flag it as 🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME instead of reasoning about correctness.
  1. State what you THINK the behavior is
  2. State what the RISK is if you're wrong
  3. Require the dev to paste actual runtime output proving correctness

  [FOR ROUND 2+: Focus on verifying the fixes for these specific items from Round [N-1]: [LIST PRIOR FIX NOW ITEMS]. Also check that fixes didn't introduce new issues.]

  Output your review in the structured format:
  ## LLM Expert Review: [PR Title] — Round [N]
  ### Prompt Quality Assessment
  ### Token Efficiency
  ### Model Selection
  ### Issues Found (with priority markers: 🔴 FIX NOW, 🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME, 🟡 SUGGESTION, 🔵 NOTE)
  ### Recommendations

  DO NOT look at any other review comments. Your review must be independent.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Wait for ALL reviews to complete before proceeding.

---

## Step 4: TA Synthesis

After all reviews are collected, launch the TA synthesis pass:

```
Task {
  name: "ta-synthesizer",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  prompt: "You are performing Phase 2 SYNTHESIS for PR #301. This is review ROUND [N].

  The orchestrator will provide you with the independent review outputs (outsider, wild card if applicable, and LLM expert if applicable).

  Follow your Phase 2 synthesis protocol:
  1. Read all review comments (outsider, wild card, LLM expert)
  2. Re-review the PR with all reviews in context
  3. For each outsider/wild card/LLM expert comment, evaluate:
     - Does this conflict with project patterns or conventions?
     - Is this a valid point that should be applied?
     - Did you miss this in Phase 1?
  4. For each comment: AGREE or PUSHBACK WITH REASON
  5. Create the consolidated final list

  Output in the structured format:
  ## TA Synthesis (Phase 2): [PR Title] — Round [N]
  ### Review of Outsider Comments
  ### Second Pass Findings
  ### Consolidated Review (For Dev Agent)
  - 🔴 FIX NOW items (MUST be resolved before merge)
  - ❌ NOT APPLICABLE items with technical rationale
  - ⚠️ ESCALATE TO FOUNDER items with reason
  - 🟡 SUGGESTIONS (non-blocking, dev's discretion)
  ### Final Verdict: [PASS — ready for merge | CHANGES REQUIRED — Round [N+1] needed]",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

---

## Step 5: Deliver Results & Loop Decision

After synthesis is complete, check the Final Verdict:

### If PASS (0 FIX NOW items):

1. **Post final review summary to GitHub PR** (see template below)
2. **If part of /start-feature**: Message the PM agent that review is complete and PR is ready for founder merge.
3. **If standalone**: Inform the user the PR is approved.

### If CHANGES REQUIRED (1+ FIX NOW or VERIFY AT RUNTIME items):

1. **Post round summary to GitHub PR** (see template below)
2. **Send actionable items to dev agent** (or user if standalone):
   - List each FIX NOW item with clear description of what needs to change
   - List each VERIFY AT RUNTIME item with the specific runtime output needed
   - Reference specific files and line numbers where possible
3. **Wait for fixes to be pushed** — dev agent pushes fix commits to the PR branch
4. **Post-fix re-verification gate (MANDATORY):**
   - Dev MUST re-run ALL functional verification commands from the original PR body
   - Dev MUST paste updated verification output as a PR comment
   - If the PR had curl examples, re-run them and paste the responses
   - If the PR had screenshot evidence, re-capture after fixes
   - For VERIFY AT RUNTIME items, dev MUST paste the specific runtime output requested
   - **Fixes without re-verification evidence are not considered complete**
5. **Go back to Step 3** with Round N+1, targeting only the reviewers whose areas were affected

### Loop Safety

- **Max 4 rounds** — if FIX NOW items remain after 4 rounds, ESCALATE TO FOUNDER with full context
- **Round 2+ is targeted** — only re-invoke reviewers whose prior FIX NOW items were addressed (don't re-run all 4 reviewers for a one-line fix)
- **New issues found during fix verification count as new FIX NOW items** — the loop continues

### PR Comment Template

```bash
gh pr comment 301 --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Triple-Layer Code Review — Round [N] of [TOTAL]

### Reviewers
| Role | Domain | This Round |
|------|--------|------------|
| TA (Insider) | Architecture, types, schema | [Active/Skipped] |
| [Specialist 1 name] | [Domain] | [Active/Skipped] |
| [Specialist 2 name] | [Domain] | [Active/Skipped/N/A] |
| LLM Expert | Prompt quality, token efficiency | [Active/Skipped/N/A] |

### Pre-Review Gates
- [ ] New dependency audit: [PASS/N/A]
- [ ] Functional verification evidence: [PASS — describe what was verified]
- [ ] Visual output attached: [PASS/N/A]

### Issues Found & Resolution
#### 🔴 FIX NOW
[List from synthesis — empty if PASS]

#### 🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME
[Items requiring runtime evidence — empty if none]

#### ❌ NOT APPLICABLE
[List with technical rationale]

#### 🟡 SUGGESTIONS
[Non-blocking items]

### Post-Fix Verification
[For Round 2+: paste re-run of original functional verification commands + VERIFY AT RUNTIME evidence]

**Round [N] verdict: [PASS — Ready for merge | CHANGES REQUIRED — see FIX NOW / VERIFY AT RUNTIME items]**
EOF
)"
```

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** — founder-only
- **Reviews MUST be independent** — no reviewer sees another's output during Phase 1
- **TA synthesis is authoritative** — TA can mark specialist comments as "NOT APPLICABLE" with technical justification, EXCEPT for VERIFY AT RUNTIME items (see below)
- **VERIFY AT RUNTIME items cannot be dismissed** — TA synthesis MUST NOT mark these as NOT APPLICABLE. They require runtime evidence from the dev before they can be resolved
- **Domain specialists are selected dynamically** — see Step 2 and `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md` for the registry
- **Always post summary to GitHub PR** — this creates the audit trail
- **Review loops until 0 FIX NOW and 0 VERIFY AT RUNTIME items** — a single pass is not sufficient if blocking issues exist
- **Post-fix re-verification is mandatory** — after Round N fixes, dev must re-run ALL functional verification from the PR body and paste updated output
- **Pre-review gates are mandatory** — missing verification evidence blocks the review from starting
- **Max 4 rounds** — escalate to founder if review doesn't converge
- **Round 2+ is targeted** — don't waste reviewer cycles re-reviewing areas with no changes

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The conversation continued from a previous session where PR #299 (Dispatch UI full-screen overlay + cover image prompt) was in Round 2 review. After merging PR #299, the user requested UX enhancements for Dispatch discoverability: (1) an inline "Write about this" button on InsightsPage for qualifying sessions, (2) a dismissible discovery callout, and (3) pre-populated DispatchDrawer with session title + learnings/decisions. The user requested UX Engineer input, confirmed Option B (overlay in-place, not navigation), approved the full design spec, and initiated `/start-feature` for full ceremony development.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Triple-layer code review: TA Insider + domain specialists + TA synthesis — loops until 0 FIX NOW items
   - Gate B enforcement: VISUAL-tagged PRs require actual embedded screenshots (not text descriptions) before review proceeds
   - `canGenerate` guard in DispatchDrawer: requires `selectedInsights.length >= 3` — entry from InsightsPage must auto-select insights
   - Radix Sheet `onOpenAutoFocus` callback: correct way to intercept Radix's focus management vs `requestAnimationFrame` (which races the animation)
   - React `useEffect` reset asymmetry: when multiple state variables are reset across `handleClose` and the effect's `!open` branch, divergence creates fragile behavior
   - ARIA label association: `<label htmlFor>` + `<input id>` must be paired; unassociated labels are decoration only
   - `DispatchFormat = 'blog' | 'linkedin'` — the actual TypeScript enum values in the codebase; spec language ("Tutorial/Postmortem/deep-dive") doesn't match
   - localStorage keys: `ci.dispatch.calloutDismissed`, `ci.dispatch.opened` — lifetime-global dismiss per device
   - React Query key convention: must include all query params (e.g., `['facets', 'list', '30d']` not `['facets', 'list']`)
   - Pre-fill logic: title from `session.title`, format mapped from `session.character`, contextMarkdown from top-3 effective patterns + top-3 user-actionable friction (`attribution === 'user-actionable'`)
   - TeamDelete requires all members shut down first — shutdown_request/response protocol

# /start-review — Triple-Layer Code Review Team

**PR**: 301

You are setting up a triple-layer code review for PR `301`. This can be used standalone or as part of a `/start-feature` team workflow. The review loops until all FIX NOW items are resolved — it does NOT end after a single pass.

---

## Step 1: Get PR Details

Fetch the PR details:

```bash
# Get the correct owner from git remote
git remote get-url origin | sed 's/.*[:/]\([^/]*\)\/[^/]*\.git/\1/'
```

Use `gh pr view 301` to get PR title, description, and diff stats.
Use `gh pr diff 301` to get the diff.

Determine the PR scope:
- Count files changed and lines changed per file
- Identify if it touches schema concerns (types.ts, SQLite schema, server API)
- Classify changed files into domains for specialist selection (Step 2)

---

## Step 2: Select Domain Specialists

Instead of fixed generalist reviewers, select 1-2 **domain specialists** based on what the PR actually changes. Each specialist combines deep domain expertise with general engineering awareness. See `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md` for the full specialist registry and prompt templates.

### Domain Classification

Classify each changed file into a domain based on file patterns:

| Domain | File Pattern Triggers |
|--------|----------------------|
| **SQL/Database** | `server/src/routes/*.ts` (when containing SQL keywords), `cli/src/db/*.ts` |
| **React/Frontend** | `dashboard/src/**/*.tsx`, `dashboard/src/**/*.ts` |
| **Node/CLI** | `cli/src/commands/*.ts`, `cli/src/utils/*.ts`, `server/src/*.ts` (non-route, non-LLM) |
| **Parser/Provider** | `cli/src/providers/**/*.ts`, `cli/src/parser/*.ts` |
| **LLM** | `server/src/llm/**/*.ts` — handled by LLM Expert (separate, unchanged) |

Files that don't match any domain (e.g., `package.json`, `tsconfig.json`, `.gitignore`, `CLAUDE.md`) are ignored during classification.

### Selection Algorithm

1. For each domain, sum the lines changed across all files in that domain
2. **Primary specialist** = domain with the most lines changed
3. **Secondary specialist** = next domain IF it has >= 30% of total changed lines AND is a different domain
4. Cap at **2 domain specialists** (LLM Expert is a separate conditional reviewer)
5. If a PR changes ONLY non-domain files, use the **Node/CLI Specialist** as general-purpose

### LLM Expert (Conditional — Unchanged)

**Invoke LLM Expert if ANY of these apply:**
- PR touches `server/src/llm/` (prompts, providers, export-prompts)
- PR adds or modifies LLM API calls
- PR changes structured output schemas or SSE streaming
- PR modifies token budgets or model selection logic
- PR adds new LLM-powered features

**Skip LLM Expert if ALL of these apply:**
- No LLM code touched
- Pure UI, CLI, or schema changes
- Provider (source tool) implementations only

---

## Step 2.5: Pre-Review Gates

Before launching reviewers, check these gates. If any gate fails, the review CANNOT proceed — send the PR back to the dev agent (or inform the user if standalone) with what's missing.

### Gate A: New Dependency Audit

Check if `package.json` (any workspace) was modified in the PR diff.

If new dependencies were added:

```
Task {
  name: "dep-auditor",
  subagent_type: "Explore",
  prompt: "Research the following new npm dependencies added in PR #301. For EACH dependency:

  1. Search the library's GitHub issues for known limitations, gotchas, and common pitfalls
  2. Read the library's README for caveats, browser compatibility notes, and unsupported features
  3. Check if the library has specific CSS, rendering, or serialization constraints
  4. Check the library's weekly downloads and last publish date (is it maintained?)

  Output a structured report:
  ## Dependency Audit: [package-name]
  ### Known Limitations
  ### Gotchas for Our Use Case
  ### Risk Level (low/medium/high)
  ### Recommendation

  Be thorough — silent failures from library limitations are the hardest bugs to catch in code review.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Include the dependency audit findings in the context given to ALL reviewers.

### Gate B: Functional Verification Evidence

Check the PR description for a **Verification** section. The dev agent is required to include:

- **For all PRs**: Build passes (`pnpm build` output or confirmation)
- **For UI/visual features**: Screenshot of the feature rendering in the browser
- **For features that produce output** (image export, PDF, file download): The actual output artifact or proof it's non-empty (file size, screenshot of result)
- **For API changes**: curl output showing the endpoint returns the expected response shape

If the PR description lacks verification evidence:
- **If part of /start-feature**: Message the dev agent via SendMessage: "PR is missing verification evidence. Add a Verification section to the PR description with [specific evidence needed]. See the pre-PR verification protocol."
- **If standalone**: Inform the user the PR needs verification evidence before review can proceed.

**Do NOT proceed to Step 3 until verification evidence is present.**

### Gate C: Visual Output Check (Conditional)

If the PR produces visual output (images, PDFs, charts, OG cards, share cards, exports):
- The exported/generated artifact MUST be attached to or linked from the PR description
- A reviewer must be able to visually inspect the output without running the code
- If missing, send PR back with: "This PR produces visual output — attach the generated artifact to the PR description."

---

## Step 3: Run Parallel Independent Reviews (Round N)

**CRITICAL**: All reviews run in parallel. No reviewer sees another's comments. This prevents bias.

Track the current round number. Round 1 is the initial review. Round 2+ are follow-up reviews after fixes.

**For Round 1**: Launch all applicable reviewers (TA Insider, Domain Specialist(s), LLM Expert if applicable).
**For Round 2+**: Launch only targeted reviewers — those whose prior findings had FIX NOW or VERIFY AT RUNTIME items that were addressed. Skip reviewers whose prior findings were all resolved or NOT APPLICABLE.

### Launch TA Insider Review (Always)

```
Task {
  name: "ta-reviewer",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  prompt: "You are performing a Phase 1 INSIDER review of PR #301 in the code-insights repo. This is review ROUND [N].

  Fetch the PR diff using: gh pr diff 301
  Also fetch the PR details: gh pr view 301

  Follow your Phase 1 review protocol:
  1. Read the PR description and any linked GitHub Issue
  2. Check if the change touches schema concerns (types.ts, SQLite schema)
  3. Review code against existing patterns in the codebase
  4. Check existing CLAUDE.md conventions compliance
  5. Verify data contract patterns are followed (if data flow changed)
  6. Check shadcn/ui and component conventions (if UI changes)

  ADDITIONAL CHECKS:
  7. If new dependencies were added, review the dependency audit findings: [INSERT DEP AUDIT IF APPLICABLE]
  8. If the PR produces visual output, verify the attached artifact looks correct
  9. Check that verification evidence in the PR description is credible (not just 'it works')

  [FOR ROUND 2+: Focus on verifying the fixes for these specific items from Round [N-1]: [LIST PRIOR FIX NOW ITEMS]. Also check that fixes didn't introduce new issues.]

  Output your review in the structured format:
  ## TA Review (Phase 1 - Insider): [PR Title] — Round [N]
  ### Architecture Alignment
  ### Issues Found (with priority markers: 🔴 FIX NOW, 🟡 SUGGESTION, 🔵 NOTE)
  ### Phase 1 Verdict

  DO NOT look at any other review comments. Your review must be independent.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

### Launch Domain Specialist Reviews (1-2, Dynamic)

For each selected specialist from Step 2, launch a review agent using the prompt template from `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md`. Use the `superpowers:code-reviewer` subagent type for all domain specialists.

**Important:** Copy the full prompt template from the specialist registry, including:
- The domain-specific checks (80% focus)
- The general engineering checks (20% focus)
- The **Runtime Verification Rule** (shared instruction — include verbatim)
- The Round 2+ fix verification instructions (if applicable)

```
Task {
  name: "[domain]-specialist",          // e.g., "sql-specialist", "react-specialist"
  subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer",
  prompt: "[FULL PROMPT FROM docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md FOR THE SELECTED DOMAIN]",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

**Example:** If Step 2 selected SQL/Database (primary) and React/Frontend (secondary), launch:

```
Task { name: "sql-specialist", subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer", prompt: "[SQL/Database prompt]", mode: "bypassPermissions" }
Task { name: "react-specialist", subagent_type: "superpowers:code-reviewer", prompt: "[React/Frontend prompt]", mode: "bypassPermissions" }
```

### Launch LLM Expert Review (If Applicable — Unchanged)

```
Task {
  name: "llm-expert-reviewer",
  subagent_type: "llm-expert",
  prompt: "You are performing an independent LLM EXPERT review of PR #301 in the code-insights repo. This is review ROUND [N].

  Fetch the PR diff using: gh pr diff 301
  Also fetch the PR details: gh pr view 301

  Review all LLM-related code for:
  - Prompt quality: clarity, specificity, output format constraints
  - Token efficiency: redundant instructions, over-prompting, prompt stuffing
  - Output consistency: structured output schemas, JSON mode, enum enforcement
  - Model selection: is the chosen model appropriate for the task complexity?
  - Resilience: handling malformed LLM output, timeouts, retries, rate limits
  - Cross-model compatibility: prompts that only work with one model family
  - Cost implications: token budget estimates, unnecessary Opus/GPT-4 usage for simple tasks
  - Streaming patterns: SSE implementation, partial response handling

  Rate each prompt on: clarity (1-5), token efficiency (1-5), output consistency (1-5), resilience (1-5).

  RUNTIME VERIFICATION RULE:
  When you encounter code where the runtime behavior is NOT self-evident from
  reading — flag it as 🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME instead of reasoning about correctness.
  1. State what you THINK the behavior is
  2. State what the RISK is if you're wrong
  3. Require the dev to paste actual runtime output proving correctness

  [FOR ROUND 2+: Focus on verifying the fixes for these specific items from Round [N-1]: [LIST PRIOR FIX NOW ITEMS]. Also check that fixes didn't introduce new issues.]

  Output your review in the structured format:
  ## LLM Expert Review: [PR Title] — Round [N]
  ### Prompt Quality Assessment
  ### Token Efficiency
  ### Model Selection
  ### Issues Found (with priority markers: 🔴 FIX NOW, 🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME, 🟡 SUGGESTION, 🔵 NOTE)
  ### Recommendations

  DO NOT look at any other review comments. Your review must be independent.",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

Wait for ALL reviews to complete before proceeding.

---

## Step 4: TA Synthesis

After all reviews are collected, launch the TA synthesis pass:

```
Task {
  name: "ta-synthesizer",
  subagent_type: "technical-architect",
  prompt: "You are performing Phase 2 SYNTHESIS for PR #301. This is review ROUND [N].

  The orchestrator will provide you with the independent review outputs (outsider, wild card if applicable, and LLM expert if applicable).

  Follow your Phase 2 synthesis protocol:
  1. Read all review comments (outsider, wild card, LLM expert)
  2. Re-review the PR with all reviews in context
  3. For each outsider/wild card/LLM expert comment, evaluate:
     - Does this conflict with project patterns or conventions?
     - Is this a valid point that should be applied?
     - Did you miss this in Phase 1?
  4. For each comment: AGREE or PUSHBACK WITH REASON
  5. Create the consolidated final list

  Output in the structured format:
  ## TA Synthesis (Phase 2): [PR Title] — Round [N]
  ### Review of Outsider Comments
  ### Second Pass Findings
  ### Consolidated Review (For Dev Agent)
  - 🔴 FIX NOW items (MUST be resolved before merge)
  - ❌ NOT APPLICABLE items with technical rationale
  - ⚠️ ESCALATE TO FOUNDER items with reason
  - 🟡 SUGGESTIONS (non-blocking, dev's discretion)
  ### Final Verdict: [PASS — ready for merge | CHANGES REQUIRED — Round [N+1] needed]",
  mode: "bypassPermissions"
}
```

---

## Step 5: Deliver Results & Loop Decision

After synthesis is complete, check the Final Verdict:

### If PASS (0 FIX NOW items):

1. **Post final review summary to GitHub PR** (see template below)
2. **If part of /start-feature**: Message the PM agent that review is complete and PR is ready for founder merge.
3. **If standalone**: Inform the user the PR is approved.

### If CHANGES REQUIRED (1+ FIX NOW or VERIFY AT RUNTIME items):

1. **Post round summary to GitHub PR** (see template below)
2. **Send actionable items to dev agent** (or user if standalone):
   - List each FIX NOW item with clear description of what needs to change
   - List each VERIFY AT RUNTIME item with the specific runtime output needed
   - Reference specific files and line numbers where possible
3. **Wait for fixes to be pushed** — dev agent pushes fix commits to the PR branch
4. **Post-fix re-verification gate (MANDATORY):**
   - Dev MUST re-run ALL functional verification commands from the original PR body
   - Dev MUST paste updated verification output as a PR comment
   - If the PR had curl examples, re-run them and paste the responses
   - If the PR had screenshot evidence, re-capture after fixes
   - For VERIFY AT RUNTIME items, dev MUST paste the specific runtime output requested
   - **Fixes without re-verification evidence are not considered complete**
5. **Go back to Step 3** with Round N+1, targeting only the reviewers whose areas were affected

### Loop Safety

- **Max 4 rounds** — if FIX NOW items remain after 4 rounds, ESCALATE TO FOUNDER with full context
- **Round 2+ is targeted** — only re-invoke reviewers whose prior FIX NOW items were addressed (don't re-run all 4 reviewers for a one-line fix)
- **New issues found during fix verification count as new FIX NOW items** — the loop continues

### PR Comment Template

```bash
gh pr comment 301 --body "$(cat <<'EOF'
## Triple-Layer Code Review — Round [N] of [TOTAL]

### Reviewers
| Role | Domain | This Round |
|------|--------|------------|
| TA (Insider) | Architecture, types, schema | [Active/Skipped] |
| [Specialist 1 name] | [Domain] | [Active/Skipped] |
| [Specialist 2 name] | [Domain] | [Active/Skipped/N/A] |
| LLM Expert | Prompt quality, token efficiency | [Active/Skipped/N/A] |

### Pre-Review Gates
- [ ] New dependency audit: [PASS/N/A]
- [ ] Functional verification evidence: [PASS — describe what was verified]
- [ ] Visual output attached: [PASS/N/A]

### Issues Found & Resolution
#### 🔴 FIX NOW
[List from synthesis — empty if PASS]

#### 🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME
[Items requiring runtime evidence — empty if none]

#### ❌ NOT APPLICABLE
[List with technical rationale]

#### 🟡 SUGGESTIONS
[Non-blocking items]

### Post-Fix Verification
[For Round 2+: paste re-run of original functional verification commands + VERIFY AT RUNTIME evidence]

**Round [N] verdict: [PASS — Ready for merge | CHANGES REQUIRED — see FIX NOW / VERIFY AT RUNTIME items]**
EOF
)"
```

---

## Important Rules

- **NEVER merge the PR** — founder-only
- **Reviews MUST be independent** — no reviewer sees another's output during Phase 1
- **TA synthesis is authoritative** — TA can mark specialist comments as "NOT APPLICABLE" with technical justification, EXCEPT for VERIFY AT RUNTIME items (see below)
- **VERIFY AT RUNTIME items cannot be dismissed** — TA synthesis MUST NOT mark these as NOT APPLICABLE. They require runtime evidence from the dev before they can be resolved
- **Domain specialists are selected dynamically** — see Step 2 and `docs/REVIEW-SPECIALISTS.md` for the registry
- **Always post summary to GitHub PR** — this creates the audit trail
- **Review loops until 0 FIX NOW and 0 VERIFY AT RUNTIME items** — a single pass is not sufficient if blocking issues exist
- **Post-fix re-verification is mandatory** — after Round N fixes, dev must re-run ALL functional verification from the PR body and paste updated output
- **Pre-review gates are mandatory** — missing verification evidence blocks the review from starting
- **Max 4 rounds** — escalate to founder if review doesn't converge
- **Round 2+ is targeted** — don't waste reviewer cycles re-reviewing areas with no changes

## React/Frontend Specialist Review: feat(dashboard): Dispatch discoverability — Round 2

### Component Quality

The new components are well-scoped and single-responsibility. `DispatchEntryButton` is a pure presentational gating component — clean. `DispatchDiscoveryCallout` handles its own dismiss animation state, which is appropriate since it's UI-only. `buildDispatchPrefill` is a pure function that correctly uses `parseJsonField` for the JSON-encoded columns and limits to top-3 pattern/friction entries.

`useDispatchDiscovery` uses a lazy initializer pattern for localStorage reads (`useState(() =&gt; ...)`) which is correct — avoids reading localStorage on every render.

The `facetsBySessionId` Map is typed via `NonNullable&lt;typeof facetsData&gt;['facets'][0]`, which correctly infers `FacetRow`. The `primarySession` computation correctly sorts descending by `started_at` and picks index `[0]`.

The `QUALIFYING_TYPES` Set is duplicated between `DispatchEntryButton.tsx` (as `QUALIFYING_TYPES`) and `InsightsPage.tsx` (as `QUALIFYING_SESSION_TYPES`). These are in sync, but duplication is a minor drift risk.

### Accessibility

**`DispatchDiscoveryCallout` dismiss X button**: Uses a bare `&lt;button&gt;` element (not a shadcn Button) with `aria-label="Dismiss callout"`. This is fine — a bare button is valid here. The `&lt;button&gt;` is focusable and labeled.

**`DispatchEntryButton`**: The `&lt;Button&gt;` has visible text "Write about this" — no ARIA label needed. Correct.

**`DispatchDrawer` SheetDescription**: After Round 1 title-input removal, `SheetDescription` now renders either a dynamic subtitle ("Drafting from {title}") or the default string. No orphaned `&lt;label&gt;` elements remain. ARIA compliance is intact.

**`DispatchDrawer` "Reset to defaults" button**: Lacks an `aria-label` that communicates *what* it resets. A screen reader user would hear "Reset to defaults" with no connection to which field. The button is contextually placed after the textarea, but screen readers may need more specificity. Low severity given the visual context, but worth noting.

**`context` textarea label**: The `&lt;label&gt;` is not associated with the textarea via `htmlFor`/`id`. It uses a bare `&lt;label&gt;` without an `htmlFor` attribute. The textarea has no `id`. This is a pre-existing issue, not introduced in this PR — noting it for completeness.

### Performance

**New facets query on InsightsPage**: `useQuery({ queryKey: ['facets', 'list'] })` fetches `GET /api/facets?period=30d` on every InsightsPage mount. This adds a network request to a page that already loads insights + sessions. `staleTime: 60_000` is reasonable. However, the query key `['facets', 'list']` is generic and does not parameterize by period — if another component queries facets with different params using a similar key pattern, it will get stale data. The key should include params: `['facets', 'list', { period: '30d' }]`.

**`primarySession` sort**: A `.sort()` on a filtered array is called inside `useMemo`, which is fine. Sort is O(n log n) on the filtered qualifying sessions — not `allSessions` — so perf impact is negligible.

**`DispatchDiscoveryCallout` `setTimeout`**: Both `dismiss` and `handleTryIt` use `setTimeout(() =&gt; onDismiss(), 150)` to let the fade animation complete before unmounting. These timers are not cleared on unmount. If the component unmounts before the 150ms (e.g., React Strict Mode double-invocation, or rapid re-renders), the `onDismiss` call fires on a stale callback. In practice this will not cause errors (the callback is `markCalloutDismissed` writing to localStorage + setState), but it is an unguarded timer.

### Fix Verification (Round 1 Items)

**Fix 1 — Auto-select insights: VERIFIED CORRECT.**

`openDispatchWithPrefill()` sets `selectedInsights` and `selectedIds` from `insights.filter(i =&gt; i.session_id === primarySession.id).slice(0, MAX_DISPATCH_INSIGHTS)` before opening the drawer. Since `canGenerate` requires `selectedInsights.length &gt;= 3 &amp;&amp; context.trim().length &gt; 0`, users need both at least 3 insights AND non-empty context to generate. The context is also prefilled from `prefill.contextMarkdown`. Two-part condition is fully satisfied when the primary session has ≥3 insights AND has non-empty patterns/friction. This is the correct behavior per the intent.

**Shape check**: `openDispatchWithPrefill` passes `Insight[]` to `setSelectedInsights` — `Insight` is the correct type matching `DispatchDrawerProps.selectedInsights: Insight[]`. Data source is `insights` (from `useInsights`), correctly typed. No shape mismatch.

**One edge case**: If the primary session has fewer than 3 insights, the prefill-opened drawer will still show the "Add a context paragraph to enable generation" hint (because context is set) but the Generate button will be disabled due to insufficient insights count. This is not a bug — the disabled state is correct — but the empty state message says "Close this panel and select at least 3 from the list" which may confuse users who arrived via "Write about this" and expected it to be ready. This is a UX nuance, not a blocking issue.

**Fix 2 — Remove title input: VERIFIED CORRECT.**

The DispatchDrawer no longer has any title `&lt;input&gt;` element or associated `&lt;label&gt;` with `htmlFor`. No dead `useState` for a title field is present. The diff confirms no unused state variables were left behind.

**Fix 3 — ARIA label association: VERIFIED CORRECT.**

No orphaned `&lt;label&gt;` elements remain. The drawer header uses `SheetTitle` and `SheetDescription` which are proper Radix ARIA primitives.

**Fix 4 — Reset `context` in useEffect `!open` branch: PARTIALLY CORRECT — see issue below.**

`setContext('')` and `setContextEdited(false)` are present in the `if (!open)` block. However, comparing the `useEffect(!open)` branch against `handleClose()`:

```
handleClose():          useEffect(!open):
  setOverlayOpen(false)    ← MISSING
  setResult(null)          ← MISSING
  mutation.reset()         ← MISSING
  setFormat('blog')        ← MISSING (prefill format not reset)
  setTone('technical')     ← MISSING
  setContext('')           ✓
  setContextEdited(false)  ✓
  setIncludeSessionBackground(false)  ← MISSING
```

The `useEffect(!open)` branch is **not** a full mirror of `handleClose()`. This was flagged as a Round 1 fix requirement: "Does the `useEffect(!open)` branch now fully mirror `handleClose` for ALL reset operations?" It does not. Missing from the effect: `setOverlayOpen(false)`, `setResult(null)`, `mutation.reset()`, `setFormat('blog')`, `setTone('technical')`, `setIncludeSessionBackground(false)`.

However, the design intent should be understood: `handleClose` is the primary close path (triggered by Sheet's `onOpenChange`). The `useEffect(!open)` is a supplementary reset for transient prefill state only. Looking at the architecture: the Sheet passes `onOpenChange={handleClose}`, meaning any programmatic or user-driven close goes through `handleClose`. The `useEffect(!open)` would only fire if `open` is set to `false` externally (from the parent, `setDrawerOpen(false)` in FloatingActionBar path). But the parent passes `onOpenChange={setDrawerOpen}` — and `setDrawerOpen(false)` would set `open=false`, which would trigger the effect. Meanwhile `handleClose` also calls `onOpenChange(false)` which calls `setDrawerOpen(false)` again — this is idempotent for state but the effect would re-run.

The actual risk: when the parent closes the drawer via `onOpenChange={setDrawerOpen}` (not through `handleClose`), only `context` and `contextEdited` are reset, not `result`, `overlayOpen`, `mutation`, `tone`, `format`, or `includeSessionBackground`. This means stale state (a previous generation result, non-default tone, etc.) can persist if the drawer is closed externally. In practice `handleClose` intercepts all close paths through `onOpenChange={handleClose}`, so external close via `setDrawerOpen(false)` from outside the sheet is not a path that exists — the only external `open` setter is the parent. But the `FloatingActionBar` path sets `setDrawerOpen(true)` without going through `handleClose`, so that path is fine for opening.

The Round 1 requirement said "fully mirror `handleClose`" — this fix does not achieve that. Given the architectural constraint that `handleClose` IS the `onOpenChange` handler, the practical risk is low, but the requirement was explicitly stated and was not met.

**Fix 5 — Remove `requestAnimationFrame` focus code: VERIFIED CORRECT.**

No `requestAnimationFrame` calls remain in DispatchDrawer. Confirmed by reading the full post-PR file.

---

### Issues Found

**🔴 FIX NOW: `useEffect(!open)` does not fully reset drawer state**

The `if (!open)` branch in `DispatchDrawer`'s `useEffect` only resets `context` and `contextEdited`. Missing: `setOverlayOpen(false)`, `setResult(null)`, `mutation.reset()`, `setFormat('blog')`, `setTone('technical')`, `setIncludeSessionBackground(false)`.

This was an explicit Round 1 requirement that was not met. While the primary close path through `handleClose` covers all resets, the effect branch should be a complete reset to be defensively correct, especially since the parent holds the `open` state and can set it to `false` without going through `handleClose` (e.g., in a future refactor or test).

Fix: add the missing resets to the `if (!open)` block, OR add a comment explicitly documenting that the effect is intentionally minimal because `handleClose` is the canonical reset path.

---

**🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME: `canGenerate` gate when session has fewer than 3 insights**

The `canGenerate` condition is `selectedInsights.length &gt;= 3 &amp;&amp; context.trim().length &gt; 0`. When `openDispatchWithPrefill` is called for a session with 0–2 insights, the drawer opens with prefilled context but the Generate button is disabled, and the empty-state message reads "No insights selected. Close this panel and select at least 3 from the list." — which is confusing when the user arrived via "Write about this" expecting a ready experience.

**What I think happens**: the button is disabled, the empty-insights message shows.
**Risk if wrong**: None technically, but the UX is broken for the intended flow.
**Verify**: Load a qualifying session with &lt;3 insights, click "Write about this", observe the drawer state.

---

**🟠 VERIFY AT RUNTIME: `prefill` stale reference in `useEffect` dependency array**

The `useEffect` depends on `[open, prefill]`. `prefill` is `dispatchPrefill` from InsightsPage state (a new object reference on each `openDispatchWithPrefill` call). If the parent component re-renders (e.g., from a query refetch while the drawer is open), a new `prefill` object reference could be created via `setDispatchPrefill`, which would re-trigger the effect and reset `context` to the prefill value — overwriting any user edits.

**What I think happens**: `dispatchPrefill` is only set by `openDispatchWithPrefill`, which is called imperatively. React Query's `staleTime: 60_000` means re-fetches within 60s are served from cache and don't trigger state updates. So in practice this doesn't fire spuriously.
**Risk if wrong**: User edits the context textarea, then the parent re-renders and resets it silently.
**Verify**: Open the drawer via "Write about this", edit the context textarea, then trigger a parent re-render (e.g., navigate away and back, or manually invalidate the query) — confirm the textarea is NOT reset.

---

**🟡 SUGGESTION: Query key does not include params**

```ts
queryKey: ['facets', 'list'],
queryFn: () =&gt; fetchFacets({ period: '30d' }),
```

The query key `['facets', 'list']` does not encode the `period: '30d'` parameter. If another component queries the same key with different params, they'd share a stale cache entry. Prefer `['facets', 'list', { period: '30d' }]` for correctness.

---

**🟡 SUGGESTION: `QUALIFYING_SESSION_TYPES` duplicated**

The same set of session character types is defined twice: once in `DispatchEntryButton.tsx` as `QUALIFYING_TYPES` and once in `InsightsPage.tsx` as `QUALIFYING_SESSION_TYPES`. Extract to a shared constant in `buildDispatchPrefill.ts` or a separate `dispatchConstants.ts` to avoid drift.

---

**🟡 SUGGESTION: `DispatchDiscoveryCallout` timers not cleaned up**

Both `dismiss` and `handleTryIt` call `setTimeout(() =&gt; onDismiss(), 150)` without storing a ref to the timer. If the component unmounts before 150ms (unlikely but possible in React Strict Mode or fast test environments), the callback fires on a stale closure. Consider using `useEffect` cleanup or `useRef` to track and clear the timer.

---

**🔵 NOTE: `contextMarkdown` can be empty string for well-analyzed sessions with no user-actionable friction and no patterns**

`buildDispatchPrefill` returns `contextMarkdown: sections.join('\n\n')`. If a session has zero `effective_patterns` and zero `user-actionable` friction points, `sections` is empty and `contextMarkdown` is `''`. The drawer will open with an empty context, making `canGenerate` fail (since `context.trim().length &gt; 0` is required). This is a known edge case and correct behavior — the "Add a context paragraph" hint will guide the user. Just ensuring this path is understood.

---

**🔵 NOTE: PR description mentions "autoFocus+select on the title input" but that feature was removed**

The PR description in the "How" section states "autoFocus+select on the title input" — but the title input was removed in Round 1. The PR description is stale. No code impact, but worth updating for reader clarity.

---

### Verdict

**Round 1 fixes: 4 of 5 fully correct.** Fix 4 (useEffect reset mirroring handleClose) was only partially implemented — `context` and `contextEdited` were added, but the other 5 state variables from `handleClose` were omitted. This is a 🔴 issue requiring either completing the reset or explicit documentation that it is intentionally partial.

All new components are clean, accessible, and well-scoped. The overall implementation is high quality. Once the `useEffect(!open)` gap is resolved (either with a full reset or a documented comment explaining the invariant), this PR is ready to merge.</result>

## React/Frontend Specialist Review: feat(dashboard): Dispatch discoverability — Round 3

### Fix Verification (Round 2 FIX NOW item)

The fix is in `InsightsPage.tsx`. The `primarySession` `useMemo` now filters qualifying sessions using two additional conditions: `sessionInsightCount &gt;= 3` (via `insights.filter(i =&gt; i.session_id === s.id).length`) and non-empty prefill content (at least one effective pattern OR user-actionable friction point via `parseJsonField`). This directly addresses the broken-state concern from Round 2.

---

### Issues Found

**1. `insights` IS correctly in the dependency array**

The `primarySession` `useMemo` declaration at line 162:
```
}, [allSessions, facetsBySessionId, insights]);
```
`insights` is the third dependency. This is correct. The filter will recompute when `insights` loads asynchronously (i.e., when the `useInsights` query resolves and `insights` goes from `[]` to the populated array). No bug here.

**2. Field names on `FacetRow` are correct**

The filter uses `facetRow.effective_patterns` and `facetRow.friction_points`. Cross-checking against:
- `FacetRow` interface in `dashboard/src/lib/types.ts`: fields are `friction_points: string` and `effective_patterns: string`. Correct.
- `server/src/routes/facets.ts` server-side `FacetRow` interface: identical field names. Correct.
- The SQLite query `SELECT sf.*` returns raw column names from `session_facets` table, which are `friction_points` and `effective_patterns`. Correct.

`parseJsonField&lt;EffectivePattern[]&gt;(facetRow.effective_patterns, [])` and `parseJsonField&lt;FrictionPoint[]&gt;(facetRow.friction_points, [])` are both correct usages.

**3. Cascade to button and callout when `primarySession` is null/undefined — CORRECT**

`DispatchEntryButton` receives `sessionCharacter={primarySession?.session_character}` and `facetsLoaded={!!primarySession &amp;&amp; facetsBySessionId.has(primarySession.id)}`. When `primarySession` is `null`, `sessionCharacter` is `undefined` and `facetsLoaded` is `false`, so `DispatchEntryButton` returns `null` on its internal guard. The button correctly disappears.

The discovery callout: `{shouldShowCallout &amp;&amp; primarySession &amp;&amp; facetsBySessionId.has(primarySession.id) &amp;&amp; ...}`. When `primarySession` is `null`, this short-circuits and the callout is not rendered. Correct.

The cascade is clean with no broken intermediate states.

**4. O(n*m) performance analysis**

The `insights.filter(i =&gt; i.session_id === s.id)` call is inside a `.filter()` over `allSessions`. This is O(n*m) where n = qualifying sessions (sessions with correct character AND a facet row) and m = total insights. Given the 30-day facets window and a 500-session ceiling on `allSessions`, and a typical user having perhaps 200-400 insights total in 30 days, the worst-case budget is roughly 500 * 400 = 200,000 simple string equality comparisons. On modern JS engines this completes in under 1ms. **This is not a performance problem for this dataset size.** A pre-built `Map&lt;session_id, count&gt;` would be cleaner but is not required given the data scale.

**5. Edge case analysis**

5a. **Project filter mismatch (genuine concern — see below)**

`useInsights` is called with `filters.project !== 'all' ? { projectId: filters.project } : undefined`. When a project filter is active, `insights` contains only insights from that project. However, `allSessions` (limit:500) is unfiltered by project. The `primarySession` filter counts `insights.filter(i =&gt; i.session_id === s.id).length` against a project-scoped insight list. A qualifying session from a *different* project than the active filter will have zero counted insights, so it correctly fails the `&gt;= 3` guard and won't be selected as `primarySession`. There is no false positive here.

However, there is a **mild false negative**: if a valid session is from the same project as the filter but the user is browsing with a different project filter, `insights` won't contain those insights, so `sessionInsightCount` would be 0 and the button/callout would be hidden. This is actually defensively correct — showing a button that would auto-select insights from a session when the user is project-filtered could be confusing. The behavior (button hidden during project filtering) is acceptable, though it's undocumented.

5b. **`insights = []` on initial load — correctly handled**

On first render before `useInsights` resolves, `insights` defaults to `[]`. `sessionInsightCount` will be 0 for all sessions, `primarySession` returns `null`, and the button/callout are hidden. When insights load, the `useMemo` recomputes (dependency satisfied by item 1 above). No flicker of a broken button.

5c. **Sessions with exactly 3 insights but all friction attribution is `ai-capability` or `environmental`**

If a session has exactly 3 insights but ALL friction points are non-user-actionable AND there are zero effective patterns, the prefill content would be an empty string (`contextMarkdown = ""`). The `patterns.length &gt; 0 || friction.length &gt; 0` guard catches this correctly — the `friction` variable is already filtered to `user-actionable` before the length check:
```
const friction = parseJsonField&lt;FrictionPoint[]&gt;(facetRow.friction_points, []).filter(
  (f) =&gt; f.attribution === 'user-actionable'
);
return patterns.length &gt; 0 || friction.length &gt; 0;
```
This is correct. A session with only AI-attributable friction and no patterns would be excluded from `primarySession`. No broken state is reachable through this path.

5d. **`parseJsonField` returning non-array**

If the DB contains corrupt JSON in `effective_patterns` or `friction_points`, `parseJsonField` returns the `[]` default. This means `patterns.length === 0` and `friction.length === 0`, so the session correctly fails the prefill-content guard and is excluded. Safe.

---

### Verdict

**APPROVED.** The Round 2 fix is correctly implemented. All five targeted verification points pass:

1. `insights` is in the `useMemo` dependency array — recompute on async load is guaranteed.
2. `facetRow.effective_patterns` and `facetRow.friction_points` match the `FacetRow` type exactly, confirmed against both the client type definition and the server-side SQLite query.
3. The `primarySession` null cascade correctly hides both the button and the callout with no intermediate broken state.
4. The O(n*m) inner filter is within acceptable bounds for the dataset (max ~200K string comparisons, sub-millisecond).
5. No reachable false-positive (broken drawer open) or problematic false-negative edge cases. The project-filter false-negative is defensively correct behavior.</result>
